</p><p>Black British people have performed well in track and field. <a href="/wiki/Daley_Thompson" title="Daley Thompson">Daley Thompson</a> was the gold medallist for the <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_at_the_Olympics" title="Great Britain at the Olympics">Great Britain</a> team in the decathlon in the 1980 and 1984 Olympics. The most decorated British athlete is Jamaica-born <a href="/wiki/Linford_Christie" title="Linford Christie">Linford Christie</a>, who moved to the United Kingdom at age seven. He was winner of the gold medal in the 100 meters at the 1992 Olympics, the World Championships, the European Championships and the Commonwealth Games. Sprinter <a href="/wiki/Dwain_Chambers" title="Dwain Chambers">Dwain Chambers</a> grew up in London. His early achievements winning a world junior record for the 100 meters in 1997, as the youngest medal winner in the 1999 world championships, and fourth place at the 2000 Olympics were marred by a later scandal over the use of performance-enhancing drugs, like Christie before him. <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Holmes" title="Kelly Holmes">Kelly Holmes</a> won Olympic gold in both the 800m and 1500m, and set many British records.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>, many have represented <a href="/wiki/England_cricket_team" title="England cricket team">England</a>: <a href="/wiki/Mark_Alleyne" title="Mark Alleyne">Mark Alleyne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jofra_Archer" title="Jofra Archer">Jofra Archer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Butcher" title="Mark Butcher">Mark Butcher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Carberry" title="Michael Carberry">Michael Carberry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norman_Cowans" title="Norman Cowans">Norman Cowans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phillip_DeFreitas" title="Phillip DeFreitas">Phillip DeFreitas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dean_Headley" title="Dean Headley">Dean Headley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Jordan_(cricketer)" title="Chris Jordan (cricketer)">Chris Jordan</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Lawrence_(cricketer)" title="David Lawrence (cricketer)">David Lawrence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Lewis_(cricketer)" title="Chris Lewis (cricketer)">Chris Lewis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Devon_Malcolm" title="Devon Malcolm">Devon Malcolm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gladstone_Small" title="Gladstone Small">Gladstone Small</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alex_Tudor" title="Alex Tudor">Alex Tudor</a> to name a few.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Formula_1" class="mw-redirect" title="Formula 1">Formula 1</a>, the highest rank of motorsport sanctioned by the <a href="/wiki/FIA" class="mw-redirect" title="FIA">FIA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Hamilton" title="Lewis Hamilton">Lewis Hamilton</a> from <a href="/wiki/Stevenage" title="Stevenage">Stevenage</a> is the current world champion, having also won the championship in 2008, 2014, 2015, 2017, and 2018. With five titles and over 70 wins and 80 pole positions, he is the most decorated and successful driver in British history.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business">Business</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_British&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Business">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In business, <a href="/wiki/Damon_Buffini" title="Damon Buffini">Damon Buffini</a> heads <a href="/wiki/Permira" title="Permira">Permira</a>, one of the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Private_equity" title="Private equity">private equity</a> firms. He topped the 2007 "power list" as the most powerful Black male in the United Kingdom by <i><a href="/wiki/New_Nation" title="New Nation">New Nation</a></i> magazine and was appointed to then Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Brown" title="Gordon Brown">Gordon Brown</a>'s business advisory panel.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Carayol" title="René Carayol">René Carayol</a> is a broadcaster, <a href="/wiki/Broadsheet" title="Broadsheet">broadsheet</a> columnist, business and leadership <a href="/wiki/Orator" title="Orator">speaker</a> and author, best known for presenting the BBC series <i><a href="/wiki/Did_They_Pay_Off_Their_Mortgage_in_Two_Years%3F" class="mw-redirect" title="Did They Pay Off Their Mortgage in Two Years?">Did They Pay Off Their Mortgage in Two Years?</a></i> He has also served as an executive main board director for blue-chip companies as well as the public sector.
</p><p>Wol Kolade is council member and Chairman of the <a href="/wiki/British_Venture_Capital_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="British Venture Capital Association">BVCA</a> (British Venture Capital Association) and a Governor and council member of the <a href="/wiki/London_School_of_Economics_and_Political_Science" class="mw-redirect" title="London School of Economics and Political Science">London School of Economics and Political Science</a>, chairing its <a href="/wiki/Audit_Committee" class="mw-redirect" title="Audit Committee">Audit Committee</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Adam_Afriyie" title="Adam Afriyie">Adam Afriyie</a> is a politician, and <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a> Member of Parliament for <a href="/wiki/Windsor_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Windsor (UK Parliament constituency)">Windsor</a>. He is also the founding director of Connect Support Services, an IT services company pioneering fixed-price support. He was also Chairman of <a href="/wiki/DeHavilland" title="DeHavilland">DeHavilland Information Services plc</a>, a news and information services company, and was a regional finalist in the 2003 <a href="/wiki/Ernst_and_Young" class="mw-redirect" title="Ernst and Young">Ernst and Young</a> Entrepreneur of the year awards.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Wilfred_Emmanuel-Jones" title="Wilfred Emmanuel-Jones">Wilfred Emmanuel-Jones</a> is a businessman, farmer and founder of the popular <a href="/wiki/Black_Farmer" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Farmer">Black Farmer</a> range of food products. He stood, unsuccessfully, as <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative Party</a> candidate for the <a href="/wiki/Chippenham_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Chippenham (UK Parliament constituency)">Chippenham</a> constituency in the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2010 United Kingdom general election">2010 general election</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Houses_of_Parliament">Houses of Parliament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_British&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Houses of Parliament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Black_British_politicians" title="Category:Black British politicians">Category:Black British politicians</a></div>
<p>People of black African ancestry such as <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Grant" title="Bernie Grant">Bernie Grant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baroness_Amos" class="mw-redirect" title="Baroness Amos">Baroness Amos</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Lammy" title="David Lammy">David Lammy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diane_Abbott" title="Diane Abbott">Diane Abbott</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Oona_King" title="Oona King">Oona King</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Boateng" title="Paul Boateng">Paul Boateng</a> who are of mixed race, have made significant contributions to British politics and <a href="/wiki/Trade_unionism" class="mw-redirect" title="Trade unionism">trade unionism</a>. Boateng became the United Kingdom's first biracial <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Cabinet minister">cabinet minister</a> in 2002 when he was appointed as <a href="/wiki/Chief_Secretary_to_the_Treasury" title="Chief Secretary to the Treasury">Chief Secretary to the Treasury</a>. Abbott became the first black woman Member of Parliament when she was elected to the <a href="/wiki/British_House_of_Commons" class="mw-redirect" title="British House of Commons">House of Commons</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1987_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="1987 United Kingdom general election">1987 general election</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bill_Morris,_Baron_Morris_of_Handsworth" title="Bill Morris, Baron Morris of Handsworth">Bill Morris</a> was elected general secretary of the <a href="/wiki/Transport_and_General_Workers%27_Union" title="Transport and General Workers&#39; Union">Transport and General Workers' Union</a> in 1992. He was <a href="/wiki/Knighthood" class="mw-redirect" title="Knighthood">knighted</a> in 2003, and in 2006 he took a seat in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a> as a working <a href="/wiki/Life_peer" title="Life peer">life peer</a>, Baron Morris of Handsworth.
</p><p>The Trinidadian cricketer <a href="/wiki/Learie_Constantine" title="Learie Constantine">Learie Constantine</a> was ennobled in 1969 and took the title Baron Constantine of Maraval in Trinidad and Nelson in the County Palatine of Lancaster.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/David_Pitt,_Baron_Pitt_of_Hampstead" title="David Pitt, Baron Pitt of Hampstead">David Pitt</a> became a member of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a> when he became a <a href="/wiki/Life_Peer" class="mw-redirect" title="Life Peer">Life Peer</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a> in 1975. He was also President of the <a href="/wiki/British_Medical_Association" title="British Medical Association">British Medical Association</a>. The first black <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a> Peer was <a href="/wiki/John_Taylor,_Baron_Taylor_of_Warwick" title="John Taylor, Baron Taylor of Warwick">John Taylor, Baron Taylor of Warwick</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Valerie_Amos" class="mw-redirect" title="Valerie Amos">Valerie Amos</a> became the first black woman cabinet minister and the first black woman to become <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_House_of_Lords" title="Leader of the House of Lords">leader of the House of Lords</a>.
</p>

<li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.designfordiversity.eu/blog/2006/03/term-black-and-asian-short-history.html">"The term Black and Asian – a Short History"</a> "In the late 1960s through to the mid-1980s, we progressives called ourselves Black. This was not only because the word was reclaimed as a positive, but we also knew that we shared a common experience of racism because of our skin colour."</span>

Formed in 1985 it is the longest surviving network of Black artists representing the arts and culture drawn from ancestral heritages of South Asia, Africa, South America, and the Caribbean and, in more recent times, due to global conflict, our newly arrived compatriots known collectively as <a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">refugees</a>." <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.blackartists.org.uk/">the Black Arts Alliance.</a></span>
